[b'New York is finally installing its promised public gigabit Wi-Fi - The Verge\nSkip to main content\nclock\nmenu\nmore-arrow\nno\nyes\nFiled under:\nPhoto Essay\nNew York is finally installing its promised public gigabit Wi-Fi\nBy\nRussell Brandom\nDec 28, 2015, 12:16pm EST\nVia Ingrid Burrington (Twitter)\nShare\nTweet\nShare\nShare\nNew York is finally installing its promised public gigabit Wi-Fi\nshare\ntweet\nLinkedin\nReddit\nPocket\nFlipboard\nEmail\nToday, workers began installing the first LinkNYC access points in New York. First announced in November 2014, the hubs are designed as an update to the standard phone booth, using upgraded infrastructure to provide gigabit Wi-Fi access points. This particular installation was spotted outside a small Starbucks at 15th St and 3rd Avenue, near Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s Union Square. 500 other hubs are set to be installed throughout the city by mid-July. LinkNYC anticipates one or two weeks of testing before New Yorkers will be able to use the hubs to get online.\nThe full network will install more than 7,500 public hubs throughout the city, each replacing a pre-existing phone booth. Once completed, the hubs will also include USB device charging ports, touchscreen web browsing, and two 55-inch advertising displays. The city estimates that ads served by the new hubs will generate more than $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years. Emerging from the Reinvent Payphones design challenge under Mayor Bloomberg, the LinkNYC project has been the subject of significant controversy in recent months. Shortly after the initial buildout was announced, the Daily News reported that outer-borough hubs in Brooklyn and the Bronx were exhibiting speeds as much as ten times slower than equivalent hubs in Manhattan. One of the companies involved in the hubs, Titan, also drew controversy for implanting Bluetooth beacons in the test hubs, which could potentially have been used to track pedestrians and serve ads. The beacons were removed shortly after their existence was made public. This summer, Titan merged with Control Group to form a new company called Intersection, and Google\'s Sidewalk Labs purchased a non-controlling portion of the subsequent company. When the project was announced in 2014, LinkNYC said it would begin construction "next year." This week\'s construction push allowed them make good on that promise just a few days before 2016. Other functionality may take longer to come online, particularly the built-in touchscreen-enabled tablet, designed for web browsing, maps, and free phone calls. On an accompanying pamphlet, those features are listed as "coming soon." Sean O\'Kane contributed photos and reporting.\nGrid View\nHear New York City in beautiful 3D audio\nVia:\nIngrid Burrington (Twitter)\nPolicy\nUS cyberattack reportedly hit Iranian targets\nTech\nAmazon\xe2\x80\x99s Prime Reading perk expands to Canada and offers free ebooks and comics\nEntertainment\nOne of the creepiest series in YouTube history is now a decade old and can\xe2\x80\x99t seem to die\nView all stories in Tech\nLoading comments...\nChorus\nTerms of Use\nPrivacy Policy\nCookie Policy\nGDPR Commitment\nCommunications Preferences\nContact\nTip Us\nCommunity Guidelines\nAbout\nEthics Statement\nAll Systems Operational\nCheck out our status page for more details.\nVox Media\nAdvertise with us\nJobs @ Vox Media\n\xc2\xa9 2019 Vox Media, Inc. The Wi-Fi\'s Hotspot 2.0 signal strength\xe2\x80\x94which will have a range of 150 feet and is supposed to be as fast as Google Fiber\xe2\x80\x94is being assessed.\nThe city has pledged to build 7,500 of the hubs in place of old pay phone booths over the next 8 years, with 4,500 of them coming in the next four years, 499 of which will be installed over the next 6 months. Expect to see a few more pop up on 3rd Avenue in the next few weeks.\nAdvertising on the screens is expected to generate $500 million in revenue over a 12 year period. In addition to gigabit speeds, the kiosks will have free USB chargers, a touchscreen with internet access, and will enable "Free phone calls to anywhere in the U.S.," according to DoITT\'s website. Take a gander at them now, before they\'re smeared in hair and feces.\n#free internet\n#linknyc\n#not today Time Warner\n#public wi-fi\nDo you know the scoop? \xc2\xa0 Comment below or Send us a Tip\nFeatured in News\nRead More In:\nNews\nArts & Entertainment\nFood\nPopular\nDashed Arrow\nBack to Top\nGothamist\nSend Us a Story Idea\nFollow Us\nFacebook\nTwitter\nInstagram\nYouTube\nGothamist is a website about New York City news, arts and events, and food, brought to you by New York Public Radio.\nAdvertising\nContact Us\nNewsletter\nRSS Feed\nStaff\nParty Confetti\nDashed Arrow\nSign up for our newsletter! While it seemed like a pipe dream, it\xe2\x80\x99s really happening. In fact, the first such kiosks are being installed right now.\nBack in November of last year, New York City announced their LinkNYC plan, which would put nearly 10,000 WiFi kiosks around the city. These would provide free WiFi to anyone within 150 feet. While it\xe2\x80\x99s taken some time to get off the ground, they set a deadline of the end of 2015 to get the first ones installed.\nToday they broke ground and started putting in the very first LinkNYC kiosks. So how are these being paid for? The kiosks will be showing advertisements, which the city estimates will bring in over $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years.\nWhile the first ones have been installed, the city thinks that it will be a couple of weeks before they\xe2\x80\x99re switched on for public use. A Verge contributor spotted one of the helpful technology boxes being installed on the corner of East 15th Street and Third Avenue this morning, meaning the city is making good on its promise to begin delivering the 7,500 kiosks that will give users access to free Wi-Fi, charging stations, a touch-screen panel loaded with information like city services and directions, and allow them to make free domestic calls (albeit on speaker phone) before the end of 2015. According to The Verge, hundreds of other hubs will be installed throughout the city in the days to come, meaning free Wi-Fi for all!\xc2\x97or at least all of those standing within 150 feet of a hub.\nThe kiosk, formally known as LinkNYC, was born out of Bloomberg-era design competition Reinvent Payphones and has, unsurprisingly, garnered a lot of criticism, as most things affecting New York City do. The brunt of that was centered around the unequal distribution of kiosks throughout New York City, but the issue was laid to rest after more than 400 planned kiosks were moved out of Manhattan and into the outer boroughs.\nThe kiosks will also have two 55-inch advertising displays that the city estimates will help generate $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years.\xc2\xb7 New York is finally installing its promised public gigabit Wi-Fi [The Verge]\xc2\xb7 City Approves Plan to Convert Pay Phones to Wi-Fi Hot Spots [Curbed]\xc2\xb7 Mapping the Wi-Fi Coverage of NYC\'s Pay Phones of the Future [Curbed]\xc2\xb7 The Pay Phone of the Future Will Have Wi-Fi, Charging Stations [Curbed]\xc2\xb7 All LinkNYC coverage [Curbed]\nMore From\nCurbed NY\nNew York Botanical Garden\xe2\x80\x99s stinky corpse flower will bloom soon\nWhat $1M buys in NYC right now\n14th Street busway will \xe2\x80\x98threaten the wellbeing\xe2\x80\x99 of residents: lawsuit\nDigital billboards should be banned from NYC waterways: lawmakers\nLovely Ditmas Park townhouse with a huge pool asks $2M\nBig reveal: $675K for a bright East Village 1BR\nMost Read\nWilliamsburg\xe2\x80\x99s quirky shipping container house lists for $5.5M\nThe home on a corner lot is made up of 21 shipping containers meticulously pieced together\nWhat $1M buys in NYC right now\nFive apartments, five NYC neighborhoods\nSign up for the\nCurbed NY Newsletter\nEmail (required)\nSubscribe\nBy signing up, you agree to our Privacy Policy and European users agree to the data transfer policy.\nThis Article has a component height of 1. for\nClose\nArrow_Path\nFastestMobileNetworks\nNeverPaytheRansom\nFacebookLibra\n5G\nPrimeDay\nNews & Analysis/\nNew York City Starts Turning Pay Phones Into Wi-Fi Hotspots\nSo begins the gradual replacement of nearly every NYC pay phone with a Wi-Fi access point.\nBy\nDavid Murphy\nDecember 28, 2015 4:34PM EST\nDecember 28, 2015\nPCMag reviews products independently, but we may earn affiliate commissions from buying links on this page. Terms of use.\nOfficials almost missed a deadline of 2015, but New York City has met its estimated timeline for deploying the first access points for its new LinkNYC network, which will give New Yorkers free Wi-Fi in addition to USB charging ports, touch-screen Internet access and, of course, digital advertising.\nLast November, when the LinkNYC plan was first announced, it was expected that the first such access points would begin to replace public pay phones by the end of this year. However, don\'t expect all sorts of access points to just start popping up at a frenzied pace. The contractor that New York City is working with, CityBridge, has a 12-year timeline to install a minimum of 7,500 access points around New York\'s five boroughs.\nOf course, other milestones are built into the city\'s contract with CityBridge as well. After a year and 120 days, CityBridge must have\xc2\xa0510 of these access points built and installed\xe2\x80\x94the specific requirements for each borough vary, Gigaom explained earlier this year. After four years, CityBridge needs to hit 4,500 access points. And if CityBridge doesn\'t get it all done by the final timelines, it\'ll face fines for missing the mark.\nHowever, it\'s expected that CityBridge will actually go above and beyond the 7,500 minimum, as many of these kiosks will be supported by advertising. Presumably, the more kiosks that go up, the more advertising money CityBridge makes on top of whatever it costs to keep them maintained and the Wi-Fi network operational.\nThe first LinkNYC access points might be going into the ground right now, but they aren\'t operational. According to The Verge, it should take up to two weeks or so to test them out, but it might take less time depending on each access point.\nRelated\n7 PCs Turned Into Furniture You Might Actually Want\n7 PCs Turned Into Furniture You Might Actually Want\nAnd don\'t expect to have the promised gigabit Wi-Fi Internet speeds at each hub. First, there isn\'t a wireless device you can use to even connect to a hub at those speeds. Second, the hubs will have different speeds depending on their location: Faster hubs tend to be located around Manhattan, and a mix of gigabit and slower hubs can be found everywhere else.\n"We\'re expanding the infrastructure into communities that have not had enough (Wi-Fi) availability. It\'s a good incremental step. No, it\'s not everything, but we\'re going to get more," said Maya Wiley, counsel to mayor Bill de Blasio, in an interview with the New York Daily News last year.\nIf you\'re curious about the coverage in your neighborhood, the blog I Quant NY has a good visualization of every single location of a current pay phone in the five boroughs combined with a little 150-foot bubble surrounding each one (the access points\'s estimated Wi-Fi radius).\nTop\nRead More\nWant Some Cramming Settlement Cash From Verizon, Sprint? In addition, each kiosk will also offer New Yorkers USB-device charging ports and touchscreen web browsing.The LinkNYC campaign also seems to be encouraging New Yorkers to download heavy files with the use of their free Internet service. For example, as part of the initiative, the website says: "Free Gigabit Wi-Fi \xe2\x80\x94 You could pretty much download Ghostbusters\xc2\xa0in seconds, not minutes."Like the public pay phone hubs, the LinkNYC stations will sport large advertising displays, which is how the overall effort is being paid for. In fact, The Verge is reporting that New York City estimates that the ads on the LinkNYC stations will pump out $500 million-plus in revenue by 2028.The website adds that in the future, the kiosks may also tout a built-in, touchscreen tablet for surfing the web, using maps and making free phone calls.This project, which was first announced in November of 2014 expects to have 500 LinkNYC stations set up across New York City by mid-July 2016.A better connected Manhattan in the New Year!\nTAG LinkNYC\n\xe2\x93\x92 2018 TECHTIMES.com All rights reserved. This particular hub was installed earlier this morning, but there is one particular caveat in which you should look out for \xe2\x80\x93 it is not working as at press time \xe2\x80\x93 what a bummer! Well, at least this means you will still have to fall back on your regular data plan if you would like to surf the Internet while you are out in the public.AdvertisingA representative from the Department of Information Technology & Telecommunications claimed that the shiny new LinkNYC kiosk which is located on 3rd Avenue close to 15th Street in Manhattan happens to be in its testing phase at the moment. It is also touted that the Wi-Fi\xe2\x80\x99s Hotspot 2.0 signal strength carries a range of 150 feet, and on paper, it should be on par with that of Google Fiber in terms of speed. Real life performance will obviously vary from user to user, so this is a case of wait-and-see.NYC intends to install 7,500 of such hubs in the coming 8 years\xe2\x80\x99 time, replacing the old pay phones. In this phased rollout, 3,500 of these hubs should \xe2\x80\x9chit the market\xe2\x80\x9d, so to speak, in the next four years, where 499 more should arrive by the time June 2016 rolls around. It has been estimated that a revenue of half a billion dollars should be generated via advertisements on the screens. Gigabit speeds, free USB chargers, a touchscreen with internet access \xe2\x80\x93 life does sound good, doesn\xe2\x80\x99t it?\nFiled in Gadgets. Read more about WiFi. ProOnePlus 7Xperia 1Android QHuaweiSamsungGoogle\nLinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s Public WiFi hotspot installation has begun in New York City\nRyan Rabea December 28, 2015\nLinkNYC New York City\nNew York City has finally begun the transformation of 10,000 archaic public phone booths into futuristic, city-wide Wi-Fi terminals.\xc2\xa0We reported last year\xc2\xa0that construction was to begin by 2016, and with just three days to spare, the first few kiosks have began undergoing the conversion.\nWitnesses on the street have seen these new LinkNYC kiosks being erected around the five boroughs of New York. When they are up and fully functional, New Yorkers, and tourists alike, will be able to connect to \xc2\xa0free Wi-Fi within 150 feet of any kiosk. Any passerby will also be able to access an Android tablet inside of the kiosk for web access, travel maps, and much more. These kiosks will also display advertisements for funding purposes, as well as breaking news alerts to keep the citizenry informed. For those of you excited for these new Wi-Fi enabled kiosks, you will only have to wait a little while longer. Once the kiosks are up and running a test wave will commence to ensure that the Wi-Fi is functioning properly across the city. After the Wi-Fi connection is found up to snuff, the Android tablets, with their added functionality, will be brought online. the App\nOur Team\nTip Us\nNew York City has finally begun replacing old phone booths with public WiFi hotspots\n+12,826\nChris Chavez\nDec 28th, 2015\nWith only a few days left in 2015, New York city is finally making good on their promise to replace old telephone booths with public WiFi hotspots. The first installations \xe2\x80\x94 provided by LinkNYC \xe2\x80\x94 went up today and feature upgraded infrastructure to provide super fast gigabit data speeds to users.\nEach \xe2\x80\x9cbooth\xe2\x80\x9d also comes equipped with interactive tablets for free voice calling with headphone jacks for added privacy, although the calling feature is still \xe2\x80\x9ccoming soon.\xe2\x80\x9d (this is beta, after all). Those who already have smart devices can connect via WiFi and do the usual, like check emails, browse social networks, video chat, or whatever else you normally do on your phone, tablet, or laptop.\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s been almost a full year since Mayor Bloomberg first announced the project, with plans to replace more than 7,500 payphones with the shiny new gigabit WiFi hotspots. But what good is WiFi when your phone is at 3% battery? Another bonus is each kiosk has USB ports to charge your devices in a pinch.\n[via The Verge]\nlocal_offer\nLinkNYC\nstars Further Reading\nFree public LinkNYC WiFi kiosks are getting Android & Lower East SideTechnology\nCity Installs First Free Wi-Fi Hotspot in East Village\nBy John Santore\n|&nbspDecember 28, 2015 7:33pm\nTwitter\nFacebook\nEmail\nMore\nNEW YORK CITY \xe2\x80\x94 The first\xc2\xa0high-speed public Wi-Fi hotspot kiosk\xc2\xa0was installed at the intersection of\xc2\xa0Third Avenue and 15th Street in the East Village Monday.The hardware behind the LinkNYC network\xc2\xa0will replace the city\xe2\x80\x99s former phone booths. Each kiosk\xc2\xa0installed by\xc2\xa0CityBridge LLC\xc2\xa0will provide Internet access in a 150-foot radius, as well as free domestic calls to the United States and a tablet computer for internet browsing, according to city spokeswoman Natalie Grybauskas.The kiosk\xc2\xa0was not operational yet as technicians still need to test the equipment, but it\xc2\xa0should be online within\xc2\xa0two months, said Grybauskas.\xc2\xa0#newyorkers and #NYC visitors will soon be able to access free #WiFi , charge a #smartphone , and make free #phonecalls -- all from a Link hotspot. Exciting stuff!A photo posted by LinkNYC (@linknycofficial) on Dec 28, 2015 at 9:24am PST\nAbout 510 kiosks will be installed by\xc2\xa0July, said\xc2\xa0Grybauskas, of which 98 percent will provide transfer speeds of one gigabit, or one thousand megabytes, per second. \xc2\xa0The city plans to install 4,550 kiosks across the city by\xc2\xa0July 2019, according to the city\xe2\x80\x99s agreement with CityBridge. Of those, about 4,000 will be gigabit speed, Grybauskas said, including every hotspot in Brooklyn, Queens and The Bronx.Additionally, at least 7,500 kiosks will be installed by July 2023. Of those, 1,346 are planned for Brooklyn, 736\xc2\xa0in the Bronx, 3,900 in Manhattan, 1,238 in Queens\xc2\xa0and 279 in Staten Island.Grybauskas said a list of upcoming installation locations wasn't\xc2\xa0available yet because technical requirements may cause those locations to change over time.\xc2\xa0However, installation updates will be provided on the LinkNYC website.The project will be paid for using the anticipated revenues from digital advertising on many of the kiosks. The city estimates those ads will generate $500 million over their first 12 years of operation.Kiosks installed in some residential areas will not feature\xc2\xa0advertisements\xc2\xa0so as not to disturb residents,\xc2\xa0Grybauskas said. While all of Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s planned 3,900 kiosks will feature advertisements, just 29 of Staten Island\xe2\x80\x99s 279 structures will.\nTwitter\nFacebook\nEmail\nMore\nNext in East Village & First announced in November 2014, the hubs are designed as an update to the standard phone booth, using upgraded infrastructure to provide gigabit Wi-Fi access points. This particular installation was spotted outside a small Starbucks at 15th St and 3rd Avenue, near Manhattan\xc2\x92s Union Square. 500 other hubs are set to be installed throughout the city by mid-July. LinkNYC anticipates one or two weeks of testing before New Yorkers will be able to use the hubs to get online.\nsnip\n0\nTweet\n6 replies, 1516 viewsThread infoBookmark this threadTrash this thread\nReply to this thread\nBack to top Alert abuse\nAlways highlight: 10 newest replies | Replies posted after I mark a forum\nReplies to this discussion thread\n6 replies\nAuthor\nTime\nPost\nNew York is finally installing its promised public gigabit Wi-Fi (pic heavy) (Original post)\nLiberalElite\nDec 2015\nOP\nSo would that mean the damned trains will also be wifi capable?\nVermin Supreme\nDec 2015\n#1\nWhat are you talking about? Mogg\n\xe2\x80\x94\nPosted on\nDecember 29, 2015\n2:30AM PST\n12.29.15 -\n2:30AM PST\nShare on Facebook\nTweet this\nShare\nWho is Danny / ShutterstockThe plan was unveiled so long ago we\xe2\x80\x99d almost forgotten about it, but New York City is finally making good on its promise to transform thousands of public payphone kiosks across its five boroughs into high-speed Wi-Fi hotspots.\nWorkers have been spotted installing one of the \xe2\x80\x9cLink\xe2\x80\x9d hubs\xc2\xa0at a site near Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s Union Square. The high-tech connection points are expected to go live\xc2\xa0following a test phase lasting a couple of weeks.\nFive hundred kiosk upgrades are set to be in place by July, The Verge reported, while the completed project will eventually see around 7,500 converted kiosks offering free Wi-Fi \xc2\xa0and other services to New Yorkers and visitors alike.\nThe hubs are designed to offer users free 24/7 gigabit Wi-Fi within a 150-foot radius, a touchscreen tablet interface offering information on city services and attractions, free calls to anywhere within the U.S., and charging functionality for mobile devices. They\xe2\x80\x99ll also incorporate two 55-inch displays showing public service announcements and ads, which the City says will help pay for the hubs\xe2\x80\x99 installation and maintenance.\nThe plan to bring extra functionality to the city\xe2\x80\x99s network of aging payphone kiosks is the work of LinkNYC \xe2\x80\x93 a group that includes tech, telecom, and ad firms \xe2\x80\x93 and the Mayor\xe2\x80\x99s Office of Technology and Innovation.\nThe idea was first suggested by former Mayor Bloomberg a few years back, while Bloomberg\xe2\x80\x99s successor, Bill de Blasio, has been keen to take\xc2\xa0the plan forward, albeit at a somewhat measured\xc2\xa0pace.\nEditors' Recommendations\nLyft is eyeing car rentals for longer trips and weekends away\nAmerican Airlines expands its fast in-flight Wi-Fi, but it will still cost you\nU.S. vs. Huawei: As trade war escalates, tech companies sit in the crosshairs\nAs Apple takes on Netflix, is YouTube ditching its original content strategy?\nPaid browsers are the future, and Firefox might offer a better deal than Chrome\nDon't Miss\nAwesome Tech You Can't Buy Yet: Illuminated keyboards and a retro gaming console\nUp Next\nWind turbines now produce enough power to energize 19 million U.S. homes\nRelated on DT\nMovies & TV\nThe best movies streaming on Hulu right now (June 2019)\nCars\nVolkswagen says no thanks to outsiders as it develops its own operating\xe2\x80\xa6\nProduct Review\nAmazon's new Fire 7 tablet will attract bargain hunters like moths to a flame\nAmazon brought some slight improvements to its Fire 7 tablet this year and offers an impressive package for just $50, but there are flaws you should be aware of before you buy. It aims to bring free, encrypted, gigabit wireless internet coverage to the five boroughs by converting old payphones into hotspot points.According to The Verge, 500 other hubs are set to be installed throughout the city by mid-July.It is widely anticipated that one or two weeks of testing would take place before New Yorkers will be able to use the hubs to get online.The full network will install more than 7,500 public hubs in the entire New York, and will replace pre-existing phone booths. Installation began on December 28, the Verge reports.The Big Apple\'s first free wifi hub has been installed in the East Village, although New Yorkers will have to wait a few weeks until it can be used. The gigabit wifi hotspots, called LinkNYC, will replace pay phones. In all, over 7500 are planned throughout the city.Once the hubs move out of their beta phase, users should be able to access the internet from up to 150 meters away. The booths will also contains USB charging ports, touchscreen web browsing and advertising screens. York finally starts to convert payphone kiosks into gigabit Wi-Fi hubsTrevor MoggDigital TrendsDecember 29, 2015ReblogShareTweetShareThe plan was unveiled so long ago we\xe2\x80\x99d almost forgotten about it, but New York City is finally making good on its promise to transform thousands of public payphone kiosks across its five boroughs into high-speed Wi-Fi hotspots.Workers have been spotted installing one of the \xe2\x80\x9cLink\xe2\x80\x9d hubs\xc2\xa0at a site near Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s Union Square. The high-tech connection points are expected to go live\xc2\xa0following a test phase lasting a couple of weeks.Five hundred kiosk upgrades are set to be in place by July, The Verge reported, while the completed project will eventually see around 7,500 converted kiosks offering free Wi-Fi \xc2\xa0and other services to New Yorkers and visitors alike.linkNYCMoreThe hubs are designed to offer users free 24/7 gigabit Wi-Fi within a 150-foot radius, a touchscreen tablet interface offering information on city services and attractions, free calls to anywhere within the U.S., and charging functionality for mobile devices. They\xe2\x80\x99ll also incorporate two 55-inch displays showing public service announcements and ads, which the City says will help pay for the hubs\xe2\x80\x99 installation and maintenance.Related: Saying All the Right Things About the Hulu-Disney+ RelationshipMotley Fool", b"New York to Build Long-Awaited Gigabit Hubs\nHOME\nWHITEPAPERS\nWEBINARS\nVIDEOS\nBLOGS\nRich Tehrani\nPeter Radizeski\nSteve Anderson\nSuzanne Bowen\nRESOURCE\nEditor's Pick\nAwards\nServices\nQUICK LINKS\nWiMAX Resources\nMobile Devices\nApps on Tap\nEditor's Pick\nBlogs\nVideos\nWebinars\nEvents\nWhitePapers\nContact us\nFeature Article\nDecember 29, 2015\nNew York to Build Long-Awaited Gigabit Hubs\nBy Oliver VanDervoort\nContributing Writer\nThere is very little doubt that we\xe2\x80\x99re approaching the next stage of super-fast internet speeds. Gigabit speeds are being rolled out all over the United States, thanks in large part to a push by Google Fiber. While the South is unexpectedly moving in the right direction when it comes to this technology, the North is also finally making good on its promises. Such is the case with New York City, which is rolling out its Gigabit Internet service after many months of promises that it was coming \xe2\x80\x9csoon.\xe2\x80\x9d\nEven better news for New Yorkers is that the Gigabit service will be available to the average citizen, not just businesses. The public Wi-Fi is getting the connectivity boost, according to the Verge. On Monday, it was confirmed that workers have officially started installing the first LinkNYC access points in New York. This is after the installation was announced back in November of 2014.\nWhen the full installation has been completed, there will be more than 7,500 public hubs throughout NYC, which will be replacing preexisting phone booths. Not only are the hubs going to be offering super-fast Internet, but there will also be places for people to charge their devices using their USB cords. There will also be two 55-inch advertising displays which the city believes will generate about $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years.\nThe construction of these hubs comes just under the self-imposed deadline. When LinkNYC announced the project in 2014, they said it would be done \xe2\x80\x9cnext year.\xe2\x80\x9d While there were certainly some people who thought they might miss the deadline, the beginning of the project on December 28, 2015 still counts. Now New Yorkers will just have to watch and wait until all 7,500 hubs are operational.\nEdited by Kyle Piscioniere\n>>> More MobilityTechzone Articles...\nFOLLOW\nMobilityTechzone\nFeatured Story\nWhat the Future of the iPhone Resembles for 2020\nApps on Tap\nPersonal Coaching App Mobilizes Personal Growth\nThe Best Travel Apps Just in Time for the Holidays\nView all \xc2\xbb\nMobile Devices\nDoes Less Shopping Mean Less Phone Value?\nBLU Products Releases Its First 4G LTE Smartphone\nView all \xc2\xbb\nMobilityTechzone Headlines\nWhat the Future of the iPhone Resembles for 2020\n6 Useful Tricks Every iPhone User Should Know\nHelpful Tips to Make Your Small Business Efficient at All Times\nWhat Are the Common Mistakes People Make When Building Landing Page?\n5 Things Your POS Should Be Doing for Your Small Business\nThe Top 5 Wireframe Mistakes (And How to Avoid Them)\nView all \xc2\xbb\nSubscribe to MobilityTechzone eNews\nMobilityTechzone eNews delivers the latest news impacting technology in the Wireless industry each week. This particular installation was spotted outside a small Starbucks at 15th St and 3rd Avenue, near Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s Union Square. 500 other hubs are set to be installed throughout the city by mid-July. LinkNYC anticipates one or two weeks of testing before New Yorkers will be able to use the hubs to get online.\nThe full network will install more than 7,500 public hubs throughout the city, each replacing a pre-existing phone booth. Once completed, the hubs will also include USB device charging ports, touchscreen web browsing, and two 55-inch advertising displays. The city estimates that ads served by the new hubs will generate more than $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years.\nEmerging from the Reinvent Payphones design challenge under Mayor Bloomberg, the LinkNYC project has been the subject of significant controversy in recent months. Shortly after the initial buildout was announced, the Daily News reported that outer-borough hubs in Brooklyn and the Bronx were exhibiting speeds as much as ten times slower than equivalent hubs in Manhattan. One of the companies involved in the hubs, Titan, also drew controversy for implanting Bluetooth beacons in the test hubs, which could potentially have been used to track pedestrians and serve ads. The beacons were removed shortly after their existence was made public. This summer,\xc2\xa0Titan merged with Control Group to form a new company called Intersection, and\xc2\xa0Google\xe2\x80\x99s Sidewalk Labs purchased a non-controlling portion of the subsequent company.\nMORE ON NYC GIGABIT WIFI\nSHARE\nFacebook\nTwitter\ntweet\nTheVerge.comThe Verge is an ambitious multimedia effort founded in 2011 to examine how technology will change life in the future for a massive mainstream audience.\nOur original editorial insight was that technology had migrated from the far fringes of the culture to the absolute center as mobile technology created a new generation of digital consumers. Today, the dream of free Wi-Fi for pedestrians of the city that never sleeps has finally begun commencement with the first LinkNYC access point being installed outside a Starbucks in Manhattan.\nBy mid-July, 500 additional hubs will be installed with an estimated 1 - 2 week testing process required before each hub is activated and ready to use. Eventually, this will lead to the installation of over 7,500 hubs in total, with each one set to succeed a previously existing telephone booth.\nWhen they\'re finally ready for the Big Apple to use and abuse, every hub will come complete with USB charging ports, a touchscreen with web browsing functionality, and two 55-inch advertising displays, as if New York needed any more corporate sponsorship. On the bright side, it\'s those ads that will keep the Internet free, with the hubs, collectively, expected to generate over $500 million in the next 12 years.\nThe LinkNYC project derived from Mayor Bloomberg\'s Reinvent Payphones competition between designers, planners, technologists, and policy experts to find something new to replace the antiquated phone system.\nBecause of a purported slowdown in outer-borough hubs as opposed to those found in Manhattan, the project has also been the center of some well-deserved controversy lately.\nNot only that, but as Buzzfeed reported back in October, one of the companies involved in the hubs\' creation, Titan, was actually responsible for instilling Bluetooth beacons in select test hubs, presumably with malicious intent including tracking pedestrians and displaying ads on their personal devices. Fortunately, the beacons were quickly removed ensuing the public backlash.\nDuring its reveal in 2014, it was said hubs would begin to appear "next year." While they\'ve technically delivered on the promise, it\'s somewhat disappointing that the first working hub has arrived in a severely limited capacity just a few days before the new year. Presently, certain functions on the existing LinkNYC Beta hub -- namely the onboard tablet controller intended for web, maps, and free phone calls -- are marked as "coming soon."\nAny New Yorkers looking forward to free Wi-Fi, or are privacy concerns hindering your excitement?\nRelated Reads\nNetflix is experimenting with \'rumble\' feedback for mobile devices\nUS adults are increasingly reaching for their smartphones to access the Internet\nNetflix is testing Extras, an Instagram-style scrolling feed for its mobile app\nVine spiritual successor Byte enters closed beta testing\n3 comments\n571 interactions\nShare this article:\nNow Read This\xe2\x80\xa6\nVivo\'s 120W fast charger can fully juice a phone in 13 minutes\nUK\'s age verification system for online porn to be delayed indefinitely\nMost Read\n42 comments\nReport: Intel will cut desktop CPU prices by 10-15% as Ryzen 3000 draws near\n27 comments\nOriginal USB inventor says a reversible connector would have been too expensive to produce\n8 comments\nAT&T unseats Verizon as the nation\'s fastest wireless carrier\n17 comments\nTwo Years Later: AMD Ryzen 7 1800X vs. Intel Core i7-7700K\nLoad Comments 3\n...\nUser Comments: 3\nGot something to say? Apple\nRyzen 3000\nIntel Ice Lake\nAMD Radeon Navi\nOnePlus 7 Pro Review\nXbox Project Scarlett\nhome\nNews\nby\nPaul Lilly\n\xe2\x80\x94\nTuesday, December 29, 2015\nLinkNYC Free Gigabit Public Wi-Fi Takes Shape In New York\nTime change at a rapid pace, and whereas it was once common to communicate with each other when out and about using a payphone, these days everyone owns a smartphone. Every wonder what happened to all those phone booths? In New York, they\'re being converted into free municipal Wi-Fi hotspots.It\'s part of an effort called LinkNYC. It\'s described as a first-of-its-kind communications network designed to bring fast municipal Wi-Fi to millions of New Yorkers and tourists at no cost. The network is being fleshed out through five boroughs at no cost to taxpayers. Instead, it will general hundreds of millions of dollars in revenue for New York over the next 12 years primarily through advertising.New York is converting old phone booths into free Wi-Fi hotspots and digital hubsWorkers can already be seen installing LinkNYC hubs in certain parts of New York, The goal is to install around 7,500 hubs throughout the city, each of which will replace a telephone booth. Converted hubs will not only serve as Wi-Fi hotspots, but will also be equipped with USB ports for charging mobile devices, touchscreens for browsing the web, and big size displays to serve up advertisements. In addition, users will be able to make free phone calls to anywhere in the U.S. using the integrated tablet and microphone (you can plug in your headphones for more privacy).As for wireless speeds, officials claim LinkNYC\'s gigabit Wi-Fi is up to 100 times faster than the average public Wi-Fi that\'s available in parks and cafes. It also promises to be much faster than 4G LTE connections, provided you\'re within 150 feet of a Link.Though construction has already begun, there will be an initial beta phase to try out some of the features and provide feedback. After that, LinkNYC will roll out additional apps an services over the next few months and "on an ongoing basis over the next several years."\nTags:\nNew York, wireless, LinkNYC, wi-fi\nVia:\nThe Verge\nShow comments\nPlease enable JavaScript to view the comments powered by Disqus.\nblog comments powered by Disqus\nFollow Us:\nTwitter\nFacebook\nRSS\nEmail\nYouTube\n85K\n12K\n32K\nNext Show TBD, Watch The Last Cast\nCONVERSATIONS\nAMD X590 High-End Ryzen 3000 Chipset...14\nMaingear CEO Bites Into Apple For...10\nXbox Project Scarlett Vs PlayStation...10\nNVIDIA GeForce RTX SUPER Turing...9\nHP Omen X Emperium 65 Review: Massive...9\nCustom AMD Radeon RX 5700 Navi Gaming...7\nStudy Claims Google Chrome Is Total...7\nFEATURED\nSamsung Galaxy S10e Review: Every Bit...\nHP Omen X Emperium 65 Review: Massive...\nOnePlus 7 Pro Review: Killer Display,...\nAMD Zen 2 Architecture Explored: What...\nAMD Unveils Navi RDNA Architecture:...\nAMD Ryzen 9 3950X Drops 16-Core,...\nLenovo Smart Clock Review: A Bedside...\nFAVORITES\nBest Ethereum Mining GPUs - LoebCommentary6 commentsComment NowLogin50%50%\nTweet\nLinkNYC Starts Delivering WiFi To NYC Pay PhonesFirst announced in 2014, the LinkNYC network, which looks to install WiFi access points in out-of-date NYC pay phones, started rolling out the first of these installations this week. However, some issues of personal information hover below the surface.\nBest Mobile Tech Of 2015: Our Top 10 List\n(Click image for larger view and slideshow.)\nLinkNYC, which first announced that it would it would transform out-of-date New York City pay phones into WiFi hotspots in 2014, has started to roll out the first of these installations in the Big Apple this week. Eventually, this public-private partnership plans to deploy 7,500 of these access points.\nFor those unfamiliar with LinkNYC, the organization is a hybrid of the NYC Mayor\'s Office of Technology and Innovation, the Department of Information Technology and Telecommunications (DoITT), and CityBridge, which is a consortium of technology and advertising companies that includes Titan, Qualcomm, Comark, and Transit Wireless.\nThe idea is pretty simple: Transform obsolete telephone technology with a modern flare that addresses the need for 24-hour, 365-day Internet connectivity in a city with 8.5 million residents, as well as millions of tourists.\nThe revamped kiosks began appearing Dec. 28. The Verge spotted one installation underway outside a Starbucks on 15th Street and 3rd Avenue, near Union Square in Manhattan. Another 500 or so access points are scheduled to appear by July 2016.\n(Image: Imre Cikajlo/iStockphoto)\nThe hub points will require a few weeks of testing to be fully operational.\nLinkNYC has noted that WiFi service will be gigabit speed, and should be useable between 150 to 400 feet away from each kiosk.\nAlthough the organization promises gigabit speeds from the hubs, a ZDNet analysis of the 802.11ac spec puts the top speed (with the right modem) at more like 40 Mbps. If the modem in the portable device is not capable of handling the protocol, it will run at the maximum speed for which it is capable.\nThe 10-foot tall kiosks will be 11 inches thick and carry 55-inch digital screens on each side, according to LinkNYC. The digital screens will carry advertising, and those ads will pay for the costs of operation and needed upgrades during the hub\'s lifetime.\nUSB power-only outlets will allow recharging of mobile devices as well.\nOne may wonder if the personal information of users and their requests might also be a funding source. It\'s a thorny issue. LinkNYC notes on its website: "We take security and privacy very seriously and will never share or sell any personal information."\nHowever, in my estimation, there is a huge loophole in that statement. As WiFi hotspots, the kiosks will no doubt be gathering information about users.\nKiosk users only need to enter a name and email to sign up for the WiFi service. But -- and this is a big but -- the network will likely be logging other data that your device volunteers. It seems only logical that some the companies involved in this endeavor may want to use that information to make decisions about which ads to show you.\nSo, it seems likely -- given the stated policies -- that aggregate information about users can and will be provided to advertisers, all in the name of targeting the effective reach of the ads.\nAfter all, one of the companies that is involved in this endeavor is backed by Alphabet -- the newly minted parent company of Google.\n[Read how one organization is bringing WiFi to remote corners of the world.]\nTwo companies involved in the creation of the hubs -- Control Group and Titan -- have merged into a newly formed entity called Intersection. A press release announcing the merger noted:\nIntersection is the result of a merger between Control Group and Titan, key members of the team behind LinkNYC, the groundbreaking project to turn payphones into urban information hubs. It is owned by a consortium of investors including Sidewalk Labs.\nSidewalk Labs is backed by Alphabet. Does that mean Alphabet or Google is gathering personal information? Maybe or maybe not. When you\'re using one of these hubs, it\'s worth noting that your personal information might be out in the open.\n**Elite 100 2016: DEADLINE EXTENDED TO JAN. 15, 2016** There\'s still time to be a part of the prestigious InformationWeek Elite 100! Submit your company\'s application by Jan. 15, 2016. You\'ll find instructions and a submission form here: InformationWeek\'s Elite 100 2016.\nLarry Loeb has written for many of the last century\'s major "dead tree" computer magazines, having been, among other things, a consulting editor for BYTE magazine and senior editor for the launch of WebWeek. He has written a book on the Secure Electronic Transaction Internet ... First Gigabit Hub Installed in NYC\nTue, 12/29/2015 - 3:59pm\nComments\nby Sarah Goncalves , Managing Editor, WDD - SarahG_WDD\nWorkers recently began installing the first of more than 7,500 public hubs in New York City offering free, gigabit WiFi access (which boasts speeds 20 times faster than average broadband).\nThe first hub was spotted outside a Starbucks at 15th Street and 3rd Avenue, near Union Square.\nAnother 500 hubs will be installed by mid-July.\nThe project, LinkNYC, which was first announced in November 2014, is an update to the standard phone booth, emerging from Mayor Bloomberg\xe2\x80\x99s Reinvent Payphones design challenge. Each hub will include free phone calls, USB charging ports, touchscreen web browsing, and two 55-inch ad displays.\nLinkNYC is projected to rake in more than $500 million in revenue for the city over the next 12 years.\nThe company behind the project, Intersection, was launched by Google-owned Sidewalk Labs and incorporates former LinkNYC investors, Control Group and Titan.\nMachine-2-Machine-(M2M)\nRelated Reads\nNYC\'s New Public WiFi Is Faster Than Starbucks\nNYC to Pull Plug on Sidewalk Internet After Porn Complaints\nWill NYC\xe2\x80\x99s Free WiFi System Spark Our Next Big Encryption Fight?\nInvestors Could Pump $1 Bn into Uber Self-Driving Cars: Report\nSarah Goncalves\nManaging Editor, WDD\nSarahG_WDD\nFull Bio >\nAdvertisement\nAdvertisement\nPlease enable JavaScript to view the comments powered by Disqus.\nDisable Cookies per browser:\nMicrosoft Internet Explorer\nMicrosoft Edge\nFirefox\nGoogle Chrome for Desktop\nGoogle Chrome for Android\nApple Safari on OS X/macOS\nApple Safari on iOS\nNote: If you are using a browser that is not listed here, please do a quick internet search on how to block cookies and tracking for your specific browser.\nThis website uses cookies to ensure you get the best user experience. Use a + to require a term in results and - to\nexclude terms.Example: +water -Europe\nTop Menu\nNext Gen Wireless Summit\nVideo\nWireline\nResources\nWebinars\nEvents\nSubscribe\nMain navigation\nWireless\nTech\n5G\nIOT\nMain navigation - Mobile\nWireless\nTech\n5G\nIOT\nTech\nLinkNYC access points start appearing in New York City\nby Monica Alleven |\nDec 29, 2015 2:59pm\nWorkers have started installing the first LinkNYC access points in New York City.\xc2\xa0The Verge\xc2\xa0reported spotting an installation outside a small Starbucks at 15th Street and 3rd Avenue, near Manhattan's Union Square.\nLinkNYC, which is in charge of the installation, expects one or two weeks of testing will be required before New Yorkers are able to use hubs to get online, the Verge reports. Some 500 other hubs are to be installed throughout the city by mid-July to deliver free public gigabit Wi-Fi access.\nAccording to the Link.NYC web site, the launch of LinkNYC begins with a beta phase, giving New Yorkers an opportunity to try out Link's features, provide feedback and help create the future of the sidewalk experience. Additional apps and services will be rolled out over the next few months and over the next decade.\nGoogle (NASDAQ: GOOG)-backed Sidewalk Labs is an investor in Intersection, the company formed with the merger of Control Group and Titan, and Intersection is part of the consortium (CityBridge) launching LinkNYC, along with Qualcomm (NASDAQ:QCOM) and Civiq Smartscapes. In September, Comark launched Civiq Smartscapes, which provides the terminals that are replacing phone booths.\nThe project has not been without controversy, including accusations that poor neighborhoods would get slower speeds because advertisers would be less willing to sponsor booths there, The Next Web notes. The city also had Bluetooth devices removed from the booths last year after Buzzfeed reported that thousands of the phone booth advertising displays were being fitted with beacons without any public notice or consultation.\nIn a statement to BuzzFeed in October 2014, a Titan spokesman reiterated that the Gimbal proximity beacons do not collect user data/information and they can only be used through users' smartphones if, and only if, the user has downloaded a specific app with the technology embedded and the user has specifically opted in.\nThe full network calls for more than 7,500 public hubs throughout the city, each replacing an existing phone booth. Once completed, the hubs will also include USB device charging ports, touchscreen web browsing and two 55-inch advertising displays.\nMayor Bill de Blasio's office expects the five-borough ad network could generate more than $500 million in revenue for the city over 12 years. Besides advertising, the digital displays will show public service announcements.\nFor more:\n-\xc2\xa0see this Verge article\n-\xc2\xa0see this PC Mag article\n-\xc2\xa0see this TNW article\nRelated articles:\nHP's Aruba introduces next wave of beacon solution\nGoogle-backed Sidewalk Labs to take over NYC Wi-Fi rollout\nNew York City project promises Gigabit Wi-Fi speeds using up to 10,000 'Links'\nSources: Ruckus is supplier of Wi-Fi gear for ambitious NYC project\nArticle updated Dec. 30 to clarify Sidewalk Labs' role in the project.\nSuggested Articles\nWireless Nokia seeks rule change for 5G backhaul Nokia is asking the FCC to change its rules for the E-Band to enable the deployment of smaller, more visually attractive antennas for 5G. by Monica Alleven Jun 20, 2019 10:22am\nTech MobiledgeX launches living edge market model tool\nAfter three years of research, which involved hundreds of interviews across 200 different businesses, MobiledgeX\xe2\x80\x99s new tool is being released to the public. by Kendra Chamberlain Jun 20, 2019 9:00am\nTech SaT5G demos make case for 5G over satellite SaT5G conducted six demos showcasing 5G use cases over satellite at EuCNC 2019 this week.\nby Kendra Chamberlain Jun 19, 2019 4:05pm\nAbout the Author\nMonica Alleven\nEditor\n[email\xc2\xa0protected]\nhttps://twitter.com/fiercewrlsstech\nhttps://www.linkedin.com/in/monica-alleven-29b13a1\nGENERAL\nHome\nPrivacy\nTerms of Use\nRSS\nCONTACT\nAdvertise\nAbout Us\nNEWSLETTERS\nSubscribe\nManage Subscriptions\nConnect\n\xc2\xa9 2019 Questex LLC. This morning, one of the City\xe2\x80\x99s first public Wi-Fi hubs was installed near Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s Union Square as part of the LinkNYC initiative, through which 10,000 \xe2\x80\x9cLinks,\xe2\x80\x9d or kiosks, will be installed across all five boroughs.\n(intersection_co / Instagram)\nThe program sprang from the Reinvent Payphones Design Challenge enacted by Mayor Bloomberg, which asked designers to envision ways to make payphones useful in the 21st century.\nAs described by the Department of Information Technology & Telecommunications, LinkNYC is a pioneering communications network that will bring free, encrypted wi-fi with up to gigabit speeds to millions of New Yorkers, and at no cost to taxpayers. The program expects to generate more than $500 million in revenue through advertising over its first 12 years.\n(Courtesy CityBridge)\nFeatures of the Link structure include digital displays which will exhibit \xe2\x80\x9cstrategic, insight-driven advertisements and public service announcements,\xe2\x80\x9d a USB charger for free mobile device usage, and a minimal footprint, which will claim sidewalk space previously lost to the cumbersome payphone structures.\nDesigned and built from a production facility in the city, the kiosks are being made for New Yorkers, by New Yorkers. The program is expected to create over 100 full-time jobs in manufacturing, technology, and advertising, as well as an additional 650 jobs in support services.\nWhile the first installed kiosk doesn\xe2\x80\x99t work yet (it\xe2\x80\x99s in the testing phase), Gothamist\xc2\xa0reports that 499 kiosks will be installed over the next six months, gradually replacing the existing payphone infrastructure, which has been obsolete for quite some time.\nLinkNYC\nNew York City\nReinvent Payphones\nWi-Fi\nRelated Stories\nJune 7, 2019\nSHoP's Midtown supertall brings terra-cotta and bronze Kingdom\nUnited States\nZDNet around the globe:\nZDNet China\nZDNet France\nZDNet Germany\nZDNet Korea\nZDNet Japan\nLinkNYC begins rolling out free gigabit Wi-Fi across New York City\nResidents and visitors to New York City will be given access to free high-speed, secure Wi-Fi under a program that will see 7,500 payphones converted into hotspots.\nBy Corinne Reichert\n|\nDecember 30, 2015 -- 01:13 GMT (17:13 PST)\n| Topic: Telcos\nLinkNYC has installed its first Wi-Fi hotspot, with the program to see residents of and visitors to New York City able to access gigabit-speed Wi-Fi for free through converted payphone booths.Users can access the encrypted, secure Wi-Fi connection through smartphones, tablets, laptops, and smartwatches from up to 150 feet away from any Link.\nFeatured\nSIM swap horror story: I\'ve lost decades of data and Google won\'t lift a finger\nYour guide to prescriptive analytics\nThis \'most dangerous\' hacking group is now probing power grids\nDear Apple, here\'s how I solved my MacBook keyboard problem\nThe program, still in its beta phase, will see 7,500 Links installed across all five boroughs of the city. It also offers device charging, and will soon provide free phone calls as well as a touchscreen tablet for mobile browsing.The Wi-Fi is free to use, with the installation also not costing taxpayers anything; instead, the company will make money through the two 55-inch digital displays for ads and public announcements installed at each Link. These displays are predicted to generate over $500 million both for the city of New York and for the company.The company rolling out the Wi-Fi, called CityBridge, also has a "robust and forward-thinking privacy policy", promising not to share or onsell any personal information collected through the network.\nThe privacy policy [PDF] outlines what information CityBridge and its parent company Titan Outdoor collects, which includes user names, passwords, and email addresses upon registration.During use of the Wi-Fi, it also collects a user\'s MAC address, IP address, browser type and version, time zone setting, browser plug-in types and versions, operating system and platform, device type, device identifiers, full URL clickstreams to websites the company provides, URL requests, destination IP addresses, configuration details, pages viewed or searched for, page response times, download errors, the length of a visit to "certain pages", scrolling, clicks, mouse-overs, methods used to browse away from a page, location information, plus "other information necessary to provide access to the services".\nHowever, the company said all information collected would be anonymized and is only for the purposes of improving the system and providing targeted advertising."We don\'t collect personally identifiable information except what\'s required to run the system," the company said."We will never sell your personal information or share with third parties for their own use."At the beginning of 2015, New York Governor Andrew Cuomo announced broadband-upgrade plans for the state in an effort to provide minimum download speeds of 100Mbps to all households by 2019.The New New York Broadband Program, at a cost of $1 billion -- half from the state, with the remaining $500 million to be provided by the private sector -- would see it provide speeds four times greater than the Federal Communications Commission\'s (FCC) 25Mbps proposed minimum broadband download speed."Access to high-speed internet is critical to ensuring that all New Yorkers can reach their full potential in today\'s technology-driven world," Cuomo said at the time."We\'re launching the largest state broadband investment in the nation in order to make that goal a reality. This is a truly bold undertaking that will improve the lives of New Yorkers in every corner of the state, and I am proud to make it a priority of our administration\'s second-term agenda."Earlier in December, Akamai\'s State of the Internet report revealed that 44 of America\'s states now have average broadband speeds of above 10Mbps.The report revealed that the District of Columbia saw the highest speed increase for the year, growing 34 percent to a 19.5Mbps average. New York, Virginia, New Jersey, Maryland, Washington, Rhode Island, Massachusetts, Utah, and Delaware all had average speeds of above 14.8Mbps.The global average, meanwhile, reached 5.1Mbps.In Australia, private telecommunications provider Telstra has similarly been upgrading phone booths to provide a AU$100 million national Wi-Fi network known as Telstra Air.The Wi-Fi service is only free to use until June 30, 2016, however, with only Telstra mobile and home broadband customers able to access it.Telstra launched its Wi-Fi network in June 2015, after turning 2,600 of its public phone booths into Wi-Fi hotspots.The Wi-Fi network also makes use of Telstra hotspots at retail stores and customers\' own homes, allowing customers to use their home broadband data allowance while away from the home.\nRelated Topics:\nGovernment - US\nTech Industry\nNetworking\nSecurity\nNBN\nShow Comments\nLOG IN TO COMMENT\nMy Profile\nLog Out\n| Community Guidelines\nJoin Discussion\nAdd Your Comment\nAdd Your Comment\nMore from Corinne Reichert\nMobility\nTPG is still king of NBN speed report\nMobility\nACMA warns TPG, Foxtel, Aussie Broadband on priority assistance\nMobility\nNBN pulls in AU$2b revenue so far for FY19\nMobility\nFederal Court approves NetComm acquisition vote in June\n\xc3\x97\nThank You\nPlease review our terms of service to complete your newsletter subscription.\nBy registering you become a member of the CBS Interactive family of sites and you have read and agree to the Terms of Use, Privacy Policy and Video Services Policy. local government\nemail\nBy\nDave Nyczepir,News Editor\nConnecting state and local government leaders\nBy\nDave Nyczepir\n|\nDecember 29, 2015\nAround 500 sidewalk kiosks will replace payphones by mid-summer, creating a network of high-speed Wi-Fi hotspots across the city.\nNew York City\nBroadband\nGigabit\nAccessibility\nNew York City began replacing 7,500-plus payphones\xc2\xa0with \xe2\x80\x9clink connection points\xe2\x80\x9d this week to create a long-planned free-to-access, gigabit Wi-Fi network that Mayor Bill de Blasio promised in November 2014.Construction of the five-borough, 5G LinkNYC network\xe2\x80\x94part of de Blasio\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cOne New York\xe2\x80\x9d push for high-speed broadband for everyone by 2025\xe2\x80\x94was originally slated to get underway in early 2015.But concerns over high-speed accessibility and push-advertisement beacon technology inside the links, since removed, stalled the installation process.Links will generate more than $500 million in advertising revenue, according to City Hall, over 12 years\xe2\x80\x94more than covering the network cost.About 500 links will be installed throughout New York City by mid-July 2016, The Verge reported, with one to two weeks of testing needed before they go live.Accessing the Wi-Fi hotspots can occur within 150 feet of a link, which also have USB ports for charging, a touchscreen tablet for browsing and two advertising displays.\n(LinkNYC)\nIntersection, the company that designed the links, was launched by Google\xe2\x80\x99s civic tech venture Sidewalk Labs.\nDave Nyczepir is a News Editor for Government Executive\xe2\x80\x99s Route Fifty.\nShare This:\nNEXT STORY:\nSan Diego Invests $11 Million in a New Land Management Solution\nCriminal Charges (213) 389-6196', b"Street Fight Daily: How Facebook Intimidates Google, Quantifying Mobile Ads' Impact | Street Fight\nNewsletter\nPodcast\nEvents\nResearch\nAbout\nAbout Us\nTeam\nContact\nNavigation\n- Select Page -\nNewsletter\nPodcast\nEvents\nResearch\nAbout\nAbout Us\nTeam\nContact\nNews & Analysis\nStreet Fight Daily: How Facebook Intimidates Google, Quantifying Mobile Ads\xe2\x80\x99 Impact\nDecember 30, 2015December 30, 2015\nby The Editors\nNo Comments\nA roundup of today\xe2\x80\x99s big stories in hyperlocal publishing, marketing, commerce, and technology\xe2\x80\xa6\nStreet Fight\xe2\x80\x99s Predictions for 2016: Part Two\xc2\xa0(Street Fight)\nWith 2015 drawing to a close, it\xe2\x80\x99s time again to look ahead to what we can expect in the hyperlocal space in 2016. We asked Street Fight staffers and weekly columnists what they thought would be the biggest story (or stories) in local in 2016. We ran the first installment yesterday \xe2\x80\x94 now here are the rest.\nGoogle Is Afraid of Facebook\xe2\x80\x99s Search Ambitions\xc2\xa0(Motley Fool)\nFacebook is encroaching on Google\xe2\x80\x99s territory by offering improved search functionality and experimenting with search in its Messenger, which has 700 million global users. Google is reportedly responding to those efforts with a messaging app of its own featuring a chat-powered search engine. Can it stop Facebook?\n10 Pivotal Moments From the On-Demand Economy in 2015\xc2\xa0(Street Fight)\nMark Lerner: From huge expansion to Asian markets to massive funding rounds to drone deliveries and new technologies, 2015 will go down as a landmark year for the on-demand economy. As we get ready to watch the ball drop on December 31, it\xe2\x80\x99s a good opportunity to look back at 10 pivotal moments from this past year and their impact on the future of on-demand.\nMarketers Can Now Run Studies to See How People Respond to Their Mobile Ads\xc2\xa0(Adweek)\nOutside of juggernauts like Facebook, marketers have struggled for years to deem mobile advertising effective, largely because smartphone campaigns lack the same measurement and targeting capabilities desktop advertisers expect. But a company called Medialets is aiming to help brands quantify the impact of mobile ads after they\xe2\x80\x99re shown to consumers.\nSidecar Shutdown Leaves Uber and Lyft to Battle It Out in Ride-Hailing Market\xc2\xa0(GeekWire)\nSidecar, a pioneer in the ride-hailing market, is shutting down its ride and delivery operations on Dec. 31, leaving heavily-funded startups Uber and Lyft to battle for supremacy. Sidecar\xe2\x80\x99s role in shaping the industry includes launching a ride-sharing app, creating a marketplace for users and drivers, winning regulatory victories, and adding a delivery component to its ride-sharing business.\nGoogle\xe2\x80\x99s Grab for the Sidewalk Has Begun with the Rollout of LinkNYC Free Public Wi-Fi\xc2\xa0(The Next Web)\nNew York is finally getting its promised 5G Wi-Fi, as the city starts upgrading payphone booths with the latest tech thanks to a public-private partnership that Google managed to get a slice of in an acquisition made earlier this year.\n5 Essential Search Trends That Will Impact Online Revenue in 2016\xc2\xa0(Search Engine Land)\nJim Yu: The search and content marketing world has undergone some major changes during 2015. The stage has been set for a shift away from producing content for its own sake. Instead, there is a trend toward the use of search and social data to guide content creation. This development will be a critical part of boosting engagement for brands and helping their content attract the desired audience.\nFormer Google Boss says Britain Beats the U.S. at Ecommerce\xc2\xa0(Business Insider)\n\xe2\x80\x9cBritain is the leader in ecommerce in the world, far ahead of the United States,\xe2\x80\x9d said Alphabet chairman and former Google boss Eric Schmidt. \xe2\x80\x9cIn the time frame of you building a small startup, the Europeans will figure out a way of building a single digital market for your products.\xe2\x80\x9d\nMeet the Lawyer Challenging the Food-Delivery Industry\xc2\xa0(Eater)\nAttorney Shannon Liss-Riordan is representing Uber drivers in the startup\xe2\x80\x99s pending lawsuit in California, but it\xe2\x80\x99s not just the ride-share app she has her sights on \xe2\x80\x94 it\xe2\x80\x99s the entire on-demand economy, which Liss-Riordan believes encourages a systematic misclassification and mistreatment of its workers.\nGet Street Fight Daily in your inbox! !!!ConnexionABONN\xc3\x89S8305 LinkNYC : New York commence \xc3\xa0 d\xc3\xa9ployer ses\xc2\xa0bornes Wi-Fi gigabitAdieu cabines t\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9phoniques...64R\xc3\xa9seau 2 minPar S\xc3\xa9bastien GavoisLe mercredi 30 d\xc3\xa9cembre 2015 \xc3\xa0 11:30Signaler une erreurAlors que le gouvernement fran\xc3\xa7ais \xc3\xa9lude la question de la reconversion des cabines t\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9phonies en point d\'acc\xc3\xa8s Wi-Fi, la ville de New York\xc2\xa0passe la seconde et installe\xc2\xa0son\xc2\xa0premier\xc2\xa0\xc2\xab hot-spot \xc2\xbb. En plus du Wi-Fi, il proposera plus tard des appels gratuits\xc2\xa0vers les \xc3\x89tats-Unis.Fin 2014, la ville de New York annon\xc3\xa7ait qu\'elle transformerait ses cabines t\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9phoniques en \xc2\xab hot-spot \xc2\xbb Wi-Fi. Photos \xc3\xa0 l\'appui, The Verge annonce\xc2\xa0que les travaux ont d\xc3\xa9but\xc3\xa9s et que la premi\xc3\xa8re LinkNYC est d\xc3\xa9sormais en place au croisement de la 15th Street et de la 3rd Avenue, \xc3\xa0 proximit\xc3\xa9 de l\'Union Square de Manhattan. Il ne s\'agit pour le moment que d\'une exp\xc3\xa9rimentation et l\'ouverture du point d\'acc\xc3\xa8s \xc3\xa0 tous les New-Yorkais devrait arriver d\'ici une semaine ou deux.\nEn plus du Wi-Fi \xc2\xab gigabit \xc2\xbb, sans plus de pr\xc3\xa9cision sur la norme et les d\xc3\xa9bits qu\'il sera possible d\'atteindre, les stations proposent des ports USB pour recharger son terminal ainsi qu\'une tablette tactile permettant\xc2\xa0d\'acc\xc3\xa9der \xc3\xa0 des informations sur la ville.\nDans un second temps,\xc2\xa0cette derni\xc3\xa8re permettra\xc2\xa0\xc3\xa9galement de passer gratuitement des appels vers n\'importe quel num\xc3\xa9ro des USA (une prise jack permet de brancher des \xc3\xa9couteurs). Enfin, deux \xc3\xa9crans de 55 pouces sont pr\xc3\xa9sents de chaque c\xc3\xb4t\xc3\xa9\xc2\xa0afin d\'afficher de la publicit\xc3\xa9 aux passants. Gr\xc3\xa2ce \xc3\xa0 cela, la City esp\xc3\xa8re g\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9rer\xc2\xa0des revenus de l\'ordre de 500 millions de dollars par an, ce qui permettra d\'entretenir et de mettre \xc3\xa0 jour les bornes.\nToujours selon nos confr\xc3\xa8res de The Verge, 500 nouvelles bornes\xc2\xa0devraient voir le jour d\'ici le mois de juillet, pour un total de 7 500 lorsque l\'ensemble des travaux sera termin\xc3\xa9. Pour rappel, en France, le gouvernement n\'est pas sp\xc3\xa9cialement emball\xc3\xa9 par cette id\xc3\xa9e\xc2\xa0et botte r\xc3\xa9guli\xc3\xa8rement en touche lorsque la question est \xc3\xa9voqu\xc3\xa9e.\nSignaler une erreurCe contenu est d\xc3\xa9sormais en acc\xc3\xa8s libreIl a \xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 produit gr\xc3\xa2ce \xc3\xa0 nos abonn\xc3\xa9s, l\'abonnement finance le travail de notre \xc3\xa9quipe de journalistes.Essayez notre offre 48h (0,99\xe2\x82\xac)D\xc3\xa9j\xc3\xa0 membre ? (LinkNYC) New York Begins Installing 10,000 Free Wi-Fi Kiosks In The East Village sherleyb\nDecember 30, 2015\nHip Hop Culture | Hip Hop Arts and Lifestyle, News Exclusives, Tech, Tech News\nEarlier this week, New York began installing its first\xc2\xa0free public Wi-Fi hub across the city\xe2\x80\x99s five boroughs, which was\xc2\xa0first announced in November 2014; the hubs are set to bring broadband access to millions of low-income residents,\xc2\xa0Statescoops\xc2\xa0reported.\nThe city will install 10,000 high-speed Wi-Fi hubs, in place of pre-existing phone booths over the next 8 years. Currently there are 8,400 pay phones.\nAlso, 4,500 hubs are expected to be coming in the next four years, 499 of which will be installed over the next 6 months.\nLinkNYC kiosks estimated one or two weeks of testing before New Yorkers will be able to use the hubs to get online.\nHowever, once completed, LinkNYC kiosks will provide citizens and visitors with free access to gigabit-speed Wi-Fi, USB device charging ports, touch screen web browsing, free phone calls to anywhere in the U.S., and 55-inch screens for ads and public service announcements. According to\xc2\xa0Theverge,\xc2\xa0the city estimates that ads served by the new hubs will generate more than $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years.\nLinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cspeed is more than 100 times faster than the average public Wi-Fi you get in parks and cafes and the LTE network on your phone,\xe2\x80\x9d the\xc2\xa0LinkNYC website\xc2\xa0says.\nThe kiosks will support as many as 250 devices with a range of 150 feet, according to officials; these devices cost more than $200 million to install. \xc2\xa0CityBridge, a group of companies from the advertising, technology and connectivity industries, will develop and operate the Wi-Fi initiative.\nThe first active Links are expected to be ready early in 2016. \xc2\xa0You can catch them by 3rd Avenue near 15th Street in Manhattan in the next few weeks.\nkiosksLinkNYCLinkNYC hubsSubscribe to The Source Online\nType in Your Email Address\nAbout The AuthorsherleybContributor Sherley Boursiquot graduated from Lehman College with a B.A. in Multimedia Journalism. Plans are afoot to install about 500 upgraded gigabit Wi-Fi access points by mid-July 2016, reports The Verge.Once completed, these hubs will also include USB device charging ports, touchscreen web browsing, and two 55-inch advertising displays.LinkNYC anticipates one or two weeks of testing before New Yorkers will be able to use the hubs to get online. The city administration estimates that ads served by the new hubs will generate revenue of over USD 500 million over the next 12 years. The city plans to install 10,000 of these LinkNYC kiosks as part of a partnership with Google, according to a report by TNW.The kiosks are designed to provide free high speed Wi-Fi within a 150 foot radius The kiosks also come with a USB port for device charging and two 55-inch digital signage screens to display advertisements.The plan to deploy these kiosks was first announced in 2014, and the first unit was deployed at 15th Street\xc2\xa0and 3rd Ave. The project has had a few issues such as accusations that poor neighborhoods would get slower Wi-Fi speeds since advertisers are less likely to advertise at those kiosks.In the future, the city plans to integrate a touchscreen tablet for Web browsing, wayfinding and information. The kiosks will also allow users to make free phone calls by using the tablet and a microphone. None of the LinkNYC kiosks will be operational until early 2016.\xc2\xa0Topics: Advertising, Government, Wayfinding, Wayfinding / InformationSponsored Links:Related Content3 ways to effectively integrate social media with digital signageH&M, wayfinding claim top spots for May 2019 digital signage storiesThe age of Machine Intelligence is here: Are you ready?7-Eleven boosts the customer experience with menu boardsLatest ContentHong Kong celebrates art with AR gamesHow to design heavenly digital signage contentWhat's your biggest struggle with digital signage?Will San Francisco ban on facial recognition affect digital signage?Get the latest news & insightsSubscribeLinkedIn Twitter Facebook RSSNewsComQi, AUO deliver all-in-one digital signageUpshow partners with Jukin Media for DOOH engagementInewvation deploys digital signage at Jewel Changi AirportMeridian awards recipients of 2019 scholarshipAtlona appoints Ewing-Foley to distribute products in Western US, AlaskaViewSonic intros 2 WUXGA laser projectorsAmazon, LG integrate Alexa into hotel TVsSee More \xc2\xbbResources[WEBINAR]: Critical considerations when transitioning from traditional to interactive digital signageINDOOR VS. The city plans to install 10,000 of these LinkNYC kiosks as part of a partnership with Google, according to a report by TNW.The kiosks are designed to provide free high speed Wi-Fi within a 150 foot radius The kiosks also come with a USB port for device charging and two 55-inch digital signage screens to display advertisements.The plan to deploy these kiosks was first announced in 2014, and the first unit was deployed at 15th Street\xc2\xa0and 3rd Ave. The project has had a few issues such as accusations that poor neighborhoods would get slower Wi-Fi speeds since advertisers are less likely to advertise at those kiosks.In the future, the city plans to integrate a touchscreen tablet for Web browsing, wayfinding and information. The kiosks will also allow users to make free phone calls by using the tablet and a microphone. None of the LinkNYC kiosks will be operational until early 2016.\xc2\xa0Topics: Digital Signage, Government, Outdoor Kiosks, Wayfinding / InformationSponsored Links:Related ContentKiosk Marketplace editor reviews 39 kiosk companies at National Restaurant ShowCustomers adapting to kiosks, but acceptance not uniform in all scenariosTaco Bell to install self-order kiosks in all stores in 2019 under its All Access initiativeSquare integration with Kiosk Pro app enables self-service for iPadsLatest ContentState-of-the-art testing: the first line of defense against fraudstersTexas Dairy Queen franchisee pioneers self-order kioskCashierless stores? Insights\nIn-Building Wireless\nYou are at:Home\xc2\xbbNetwork Infrastructure\xc2\xbbWi-Fi\xc2\xbbFree public Wi-Fi comes to New York\nSPONSORED CHANNELS\nQualcomm 5G Insights\nPublic Safety\nFree public Wi-Fi comes to New York\n0\nBy\nMartha DeGrasse\non\nDecember 30, 2015\nWi-Fi\nClick to share on Facebook (Opens in new window)Click to share on LinkedIn (Opens in new window)Click to share on Twitter (Opens in new window)New York City has made good on its pledge to begin construction of its free public Wi-Fi network in 2015. Installation began this week on LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s first public access points at 15th Street and 3rd Avenue, near Union Square.\nLinkNYC access points promise gigabit-per-second speeds, but the bandwidth will be shared by all users who connect to the access point at any given time. Since the Wi-Fi access will be free, it\xe2\x80\x99s a fair bet large numbers of New Yorkers will connect once the network is live.\nThe city is installing the Wi-Fi access points in kiosks at spots that previously housed public phone booths, and wants to sell advertising on the sides of the kiosks. The city has projected the revenue from advertising will exceed the cost of deploying the Wi-Fi hot spots.\nIn addition, New York may have the opportunity to use the kiosks to house small cells installed by wireless carriers and their contractors. The carriers and tower companies would rent the space from the city, providing another potential source of revenue.\nLinkNYC is a for-profit venture of CityBridge, a consortium of four companies that signed a 12-year, $200 million contract with the city. The four CityBridge partners are Wi-Fi chipmaker Qualcomm; Titan, which is an outdoor advertising company; Comark, which is building the kiosks; and Control Group, which, as its name suggests, is overseeing the project. Each partner reportedly owns roughly 25% of the venture.\nThe Wi-Fi access points will connect to fiber supported by Transit Wireless, the fiber provider for the distributed antenna system in New York\xe2\x80\x99s subway. Transit Wireless is majority owned by Broadcast Australia, and was formed to help New York\xe2\x80\x99s Metropolitan Transit Authority provide wireless service underground.\nThe smart kiosks are being designed by a company called Antenna Design, which has also designed hardware and screen-interfaces for various automated ticket vending machines for MTA and has designed three new fleets of subway cars.\nFollow me on Twitter.\nClick to share on Facebook (Opens in new window)Click to share on LinkedIn (Opens in new window)Click to share on Twitter (Opens in new window)\nRelated Posts\nQualcomm Transit Wireless wi-fi\nAbout Author\nMartha DeGrasse\nWebsite\nTwitter\nLinkedIn\nMartha DeGrasse is the publisher of Network Builder Reports (nbreports.com).\nAt RCR, Martha authored more than 20 in-depth feature reports and more than 2,400 news articles. She also created the Mobile Minute and the 5 Things to Know Today series. Prior to joining RCR Wireless News, Martha produced business and technology news for CNN and Dow Jones in New York and managed the online editorial group at Hoover\xe2\x80\x99s Online before taking a number of years off to be at home when her children were young. Martha is the board president of Austin\'s Trinity Center and is a member of the Women\'s Wireless Leadership Forum.\nRelated Posts\nMay 30, 2019\n0\nNXP to pay $1.76 billion for Marvell\xe2\x80\x99s
