Will others follow suit?\nThe city plans to provide up to 10,000 hotspots over the next decade, replacing phonebooths with hi-tech kiosks. The first hubs were installed this week.\nMelanie Stetson Freeman/CSM staff/File\nA woman works on her computer at a sidewalk cafe on a spring day on the Upper West Side of Manhattan, on May 6, 2015. New York is beginning a decade-long project aimed at offering free Wi-Fi access throughout the city.\nLoading...\nDecember 30, 2015\nBy\nMolly Jackson\nStaff\n@jacksonmollye1\nThe first of 10,000 free public Wi-Fi kiosks was installed in New York City on Monday, the start of a decade-long project reflecting many leaders\' growing conviction that the Internet is a fundamental right.LinkNYC installed one of the first hubs near the corner of 3rd Avenue and 15th Street, according to Gothamist, although its wireless was still in testing. Once up and running, the sleek kiosks\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 thin charging centers with two 55-inch touchscreens\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 promise to deliver 2.0 signal strength for a 150-foot radius, at minimum, forming the largest, fastest municipal network in the world.\xc2\xa0The hubs will also provide USB chargers, touchscreen Internet access, free phone calls anywhere in the US, public service announcements\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 and lots of ads. According to the city\'s Department of Information Technology & Telecommunications, $500 million in ad revenue should come in within 12 years. New York is promoting the project as "no cost to taxpayers."\nJust happened to walk by the first #LinkNYC installation today. So exciting to see! @doberman @frostenson @LinkNYC pic.twitter.com/QHGO6KYQpz\xe2\x80\x94 Phi-Hong Ha (@pdh3) December 28, 2015\nThe first 500 hubs will be up within 6 months, with 4,500 within 4 years, and scattered throughout New York\'s five boroughs. The city has denied reports that advertisers\' anticipated lower interest in poorer neighborhoods would hurt Internet speed.\xc2\xa0While many New Yorkers were excited they\'d no longer have to buy a cup of coffee to access Wi-Fi, others voiced concern over public networks\' security.\xc2\xa0"There\xe2\x80\x99s always a chance that someone may compromise the system that runs the wireless network or just somebody sets up a wireless network and fools you into connecting with it," Kaspersky Lab senior security researcher Patrick Nielsen told Gothamist.\nHabitat meets profit as ranchers restore native prairiesBut city officials, who point out that the system will use encryption, say that\'s a glass-half-empty attitude towards a major urban innovation that will also help keep the public informed about things like transportation schedules and public notifications.One major investor in Intersection, a merger of the two companies delivering LinkNYC, is Google\'s Sidewalk Labs. CEO Dan Doctoroff, who previously worked for former Mayor Michael Bloomberg, believes the program is a step forward for not just virtual connectivity, but "civic engagement."\xc2\xa0"One of the great things about New York is that when people see things happening in New York, they tend to focus on it and often emulate it," he told Fast Company.\xc2\xa0Mayor Bill De Blasio has made improved Internet access a priority, introducing free broadband in several of the city\'s poorest public housing developments and investing $70 million in a decade-long effort to make access more affordable. The administration has cited studies from the Center for Economic Opportunity which found that more than one third of households under the poverty line do not have Internet access at home.\xc2\xa0"It\'s no secret I consider income inequality the greatest challenge of our time. And whether you\'re my age or my teenage son Dante\'s, it\'s clear:\xc2\xa0the Internet has become fundamental to solving it,"\xc2\xa0the Mayor wrote in a February op-ed, noting its pivotal role in education, job-seeking, and business. "Like electricity in the 1800s, the Internet is now an essential building block of economic opportunity."\xc2\xa0At the global level, however, not everyone is thrilled with increasing momentum to recognize the Internet as a human right.Vinton G. Cerf, a prize-winning Internet pioneer who now serves as Google\'s "Chief Internet Evangelist," has argued that enshrining Internet access confuses means for ends. "Technology is an enabler of rights, not a right itself," he wrote in The New York Times, contending that the Internet was not "among the things we as humans need in order to lead healthy, meaningful lives, like freedom from torture or freedom of conscience," his criteria for "human rights."Federal Communications Commission member Michael O\'Rielly has also protested framing the Internet as a basic right, calling the idea "ludicrous." "It is important to note that Internet access is not a necessity in the day-to-day lives of Americans," he said at an industry talk in June.\nGet the Monitor Stories you care about delivered to your inbox.\nBy signing up, you agree to our Privacy Policy.\nMany countries say it is a basic right, however, and the United Nations has moved\xc2\xa0towards greater protections for Internet users, especially after seeing its pivotal role in protest movements around the world, such as Arab Spring.In 2011, a UN report said that disconnecting people from service was a violation of human rights, and some universal Internet-advocates have interpreted Article 19 of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights as further support for their position:Everyone has the right to freedom of opinion and expression; this right includes freedom to \xe2\x80\xa6 seek, receive and impart information and ideas through any media and regardless of frontiers.\nRelated stories\nForeign companies that beat Silicon Valley at its own game\nFacebook in India: Can Mark Zuckerberg\'s plan really help the poor?\nIncome inequality begins to reshape holiday shopping\nAs more Americans go smartphone-only, high-speed Internet becomes a luxury\nShare this article\nCopy link\nLink copied.\n\xc3\x97\nNext Up\nHabitat meets profit as ranchers restore native prairies\n\xe2\x80\x98He will eat a half-truth teller alive\xe2\x80\x99: Marianne Williamson takes on Trump\nPelosi on impeachment: \xe2\x80\x98This isn\xe2\x80\x99t about politics\xe2\x80\x99\n2020 race: The one thing 23 Democrats aren\xe2\x80\x99t talking about\nThe Explainer\nCan the US protect the Persian Gulf if Iran wants to target tankers?\nWhy this company wants your old underwear\nof\nstories this month\n>\nGet unlimited stories\nYou\'ve read\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0of\xc2\xa05\xc2\xa0free articles.\nSubscribe to continue.\nUnlimited digital access $11/month.\nGet unlimited Monitor journalism.\nLearn more\nUnlimited digital access $11/month.\nAlready a subscriber? This isn't a relic you'll be sorry to see go, though.The once ubiquitous payphone that dotted New York City's streets, and streets in towns and cities around the world, are being replaced. In fact, if you're a frequent traveler, or a New York resident, you'll be able to find Wi-Fi hotspots where payphones used to be.\nLinkNYC is replacing those old coin-operated phones with super high-speed, gigabyte Wi-Fi hotspots call CityBridge. In fact, just this week it installed its first one. Eventually, there will be 7,500 LinkNYC Wi-Fi hotspots around the city.You'll be able to connect to the Internet for free from your Internet-connected smartphone, tablet, computer, or smartwatch. You don't have to stand at the Wi-Fi hotspots, either. You can access the free Wi-Fi from 150 feet away.But, unlike old payphones, you'll want to get up close to LinkNYC's Wi-Fi hotspots. They'll have charging stations, which are lifesavers for travelers. And, in time, they'll have touch-screen tablets, so you can search online for places to eat, get theater reviews and make free phone calls.Next page: New York's ambitious broadband plans; the catch\nContinued on next page12Next View All\nFEED YOUR BRAIN\nJoin the 3.6 million subscribers already getting the latest and greatest in the tech world right in their inbox.\nSUBSCRIBE\nLeave a comment\nView Comments ()\nPrevious Happening Now\nThis new Facebook hoax is why you're seeing unicorns in your News Feed\nNext Happening Now\nThis priest rode a hoverboard during mass. Eventually, 7,500 former phone booths will be part of LinkNYC, according to a report.\nBy Jeff Goldman | NJ Advance Media for NJ.com\nNEW YORK\xc2\xa0-- About 7,500 New York City\nphone booths will eventually be converted to free public WiFi spots, according to a report.The first 500 LinkNYC hubs\xc2\xa0are expected to be finished by in mid-July, TheVerge.com said.Each will hold\xc2\xa0USB device charging ports and include touchscreen web browsing and two 55-inch advertising displays. They're expected to bring in more than $500 million in advertising revenue in the next 12 years and not cost city taxpayers a dime.\nAt some point users will be also be able to make\xc2\xa0free phone calls and access city services, maps and directions.The Wi-Fi will accessible from up to 150 feet away and is expected to be up to 10 times faster\xc2\xa0than Wi-Fi available in cafes and the LTE network on your phone, LinkNYC says.CityBridge\xc2\xa0won the Reinvent Payphones Design Challenge last year.The Wi-Fi spots are collectively known as\xc2\xa0LinkNYC.Jeff Goldman may be reached at\xc2\xa0jeff_goldman@njadvancemedia.com. The plan will create a first-of-its-kind communications network across the five boroughs with new structures called Links \xe2\x80\x94 providing super fast WiFi to millions of New Yorkers and visitors.\nAnd that could include famously mobile small business owners who may be in town for a business meeting or event and need quick free Internet or recharging for a device.\nThe new hubs will be equipped with free services like high-speed WiFi, phone calls, a tablet for web browsing and a device charger for anyone living in or visiting New York City to use. Features are free to the public. They also come at no cost to taxpayers.\nInstead, the system will use 55-inch advertising displays to serve that will not only pay for the service, but is also projected to generate $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years.\nThe launch of LinkNYC will soon begin with a beta phase, giving New Yorkers an early opportunity to try out features and provide feedback so developers can improve the overall experience. Additional apps and services will be rolled out over the next few months and over the next decade.\nIn an official release, Mayor De Blasio called expanded broadband access \xe2\x80\x9cessential for everything we need to do to be a fair and just city,\xe2\x80\x9d adding that the system would be \xe2\x80\x9cthe fastest and largest municipal WiFi network in the world,\xe2\x80\x9d\nLinkNYC offers gigabit WiFi speed which in perspective is up to 100 times faster than the average public connection you get from your favorite cafe and the LTE phone carrier on your phone. This allows you access to the signal with any WiFi enabled device: smart phone, tablet, laptop and even your smart watch up to 150 feet from each LinkNYC.\nSo it\xe2\x80\x99s hoped the new service will provide free phone service, Internet browsing, easy access to 911 and 311 calls and free cell charging.\nOf course, it\xe2\x80\x99s no news that public WiFi networks are not secured. In fact, a study by online security experts Risk Based Security recently put those risks into perspective.\nIn the report, the firm estimates 822 million records were exposed globally in 2013 alone. These records run the gambit including\xc2\xa0credit card numbers, birth dates, medical information, phone numbers, social security numbers, addresses, user names, emails, names and passwords.\nWhat \xc2\xa0security measures will LinkNYC put in place to protect the security of users logging on to a WiFi network encompassing one of the busiest metropolitan areas \xc2\xa0in \xc2\xa0the world?\nWhile small business owners on the go may adore the convenience of being able to log on from anywhere in the city or when on the road, the question remains.\nWill you be compromising sensitive business information or even personal data on your devices simply by signing in?\nPayphone Photo via Shutterstock\n1 Comment \xe2\x96\xbc\n2015-12-31\nEditor\'s Picks\nFascinating Predictions about Facebook Messenger Marketing That Can Help Your Business Grow\nGive Us 8 Minutes, We\'ll Give You 18 Facebook Messenger Chatbot Tools your Business Needs\nAmazon Says It Has Released 50 New Tools for Small Business Sellers\nLisa Froelings\nLinkedInGoogle PlusFacebookTwitter\nLisa is a Staff Writer for Small Business Trends focusing on marketing technology, productivity and general small business news. All rights reserved.\n"Small Business Trends" is a registered trademark.\nPowered by\nSubscribe to our Newsletter\nSubmit', b'New York City is Replacing Payphones with WiFi Hubs | TalentRefresh | Small Business Ideas & Resources for Entrepreneurs\nTalentRefresh | Small Business Ideas & Resources for Entrepreneurs\nEntrepreneurial Empowerment, Enrichment & Encouragement\nSearch\nMain menu\nSkip to primary content\nSkip to secondary content\nHomeDriveAdvertiseContact Us\nPost navigation\n\xe2\x86\x90 Previous\nNext \xe2\x86\x92\nNew York City is Replacing Payphones with WiFi Hubs\nPosted on December 31, 2015\nby\nLisa Froelings\nIn an effort to keep up with the demand for fast public WiFi, New York City Mayor Bill de Blasio and LinkNYC have\xc2\xa0teamed up to replace 7,500 pay \xc2\xa0phones with WiFi hubs. The plan will create a first-of-its-kind communications network across the five boroughs with new structures called Links \xe2\x80\x94 providing super fast WiFi to millions of New Yorkers and visitors.\nAnd that could include famously mobile small business owners who may be in town for a business meeting or event and need quick free Internet or recharging for a device.\nThe new hubs will be equipped with free services like high-speed WiFi, phone calls, a tablet for web browsing and a device charger for anyone living in or visiting New York City to use. Features are free to the public. They also come at no cost to taxpayers.\nInstead, the system will use 55-inch advertising displays to serve that will not only pay for the service, but is also projected to generate $500 million in revenue over the next 12 years.\nThe launch of LinkNYC will soon begin with a beta phase, giving New Yorkers an early opportunity to try out features and provide feedback so developers can improve the overall experience. Additional apps and services will be rolled out over the next few months and over the next decade.\nIn an official release, Mayor De Blasio called expanded broadband access \xe2\x80\x9cessential for everything we need to do to be a fair and just city,\xe2\x80\x9d adding that the system would be \xe2\x80\x9cthe fastest and largest municipal WiFi network in the world,\xe2\x80\x9d\nLinkNYC offers gigabit WiFi speed which in perspective is up to 100 times faster than the average public connection you get from your favorite cafe and the LTE phone carrier on your phone. This allows you access to the signal with any WiFi enabled device: smart phone, tablet, laptop and even your smart watch up to 150 feet from each LinkNYC.\nSo it\xe2\x80\x99s hoped the new service will provide free phone service, Internet browsing, easy access to 911 and 311 calls and free cell charging.\nOf course, it\xe2\x80\x99s no news that public WiFi networks are not secured. In fact, a study by online security experts Risk Based Security recently put those risks into perspective.\nIn the report, the firm estimates 822 million records were exposed globally in 2013 alone. These records run the gambit including\xc2\xa0credit card numbers, birth dates, medical information, phone numbers, social security numbers, addresses, user names, emails, names and passwords.\nWhat \xc2\xa0security measures will LinkNYC put in place to protect the security of users logging on to a WiFi network encompassing one of the busiest metropolitan areas \xc2\xa0in \xc2\xa0the world?\nWhile small business owners on the go may adore the convenience of being able to log on from anywhere in the city or when on the road, the question remains.\nWill you be compromising sensitive business information or even personal data on your devices simply by signing in?\nPayphone Photo via Shutterstock\nThis article, \xe2\x80\x9cNew York City is Replacing Payphones with WiFi Hubs\xe2\x80\x9d was first published on Small Business Trends\nThis entry was posted in Technology Trends by Lisa Froelings. Center\nWebinars\nEvents\nSponsors\nSubscribe\nMarketing Opportunities\nAdvertising Placements\nEditorial Opportunities\nPipeline Memberships\nNews Center\nNew York Calling: Program To Turn Phone Booths Into Wi-Fi Hotspots in BetaLinkNYC begins rolling out free gigabit Wi-Fi across New York CityLinkNYC has begun beta-testing its program to turn 7500 New York City phone booths into Wi-Fi hotspots with encrypted secure connectivity through smartphones tablets laptops and smartwatches from up to 150 feet away\nLinkNYC has installed its\xc2\xa0first Wi-Fi hotspot, with the program to see residents of and visitors to New York City able to access gigabit-speed Wi-Fi for free through converted payphone booths.Users can access the encrypted, secure Wi-Fi connection through smartphones, tablets, laptops, and smartwatches from up to 150 feet away from any Link.The program, still in its beta phase, will see 7,500 Links installed across all five boroughs of the city. It also offers device charging, and will soon provide free phone calls as well as a touchscreen tablet for mobile browsing.The Wi-Fi is free to use, with the installation also not costing taxpayers anything; instead, the company will make money through the two 55-inch digital displays for ads and public announcements installed at each Link. These displays are predicted to generate over $500 million both for the city of New York and for the company.The company rolling out the Wi-Fi, called CityBridge, also has a "robust and forward-thinking privacy policy", promising not to share or onsell any personal information collected through the network.The\xc2\xa0privacy policy\xc2\xa0outlines what information CityBridge and its parent company Titan Outdoor collects, which includes user names, passwords, and email addresses upon registration.During use of the Wi-Fi, it also collects a user\'s MAC address, IP address, browser type and version, time zone setting, browser plug-in types and versions, operating system and platform, device type, device identifiers, full URL clickstreams to websites the company provides, URL requests, destination IP addresses, configuration details, pages viewed or searched for, page response times, download errors, the length of a visit to "certain pages", scrolling, clicks, mouse-overs, methods used to browse away from a page, location information, plus "other information necessary to provide access to the services".However, the company said all information collected would be anonymized and is only for the purposes of improving the system and providing targeted advertising.\n"We don\'t collect personally identifiable information except what\'s required to run the system," the company said."We will never sell your personal information or share with third parties for their own use."At the beginning of 2015, New York Governor Andrew Cuomo announced broadband-upgrade plans for the state in an effort to provide minimum download speeds of\xc2\xa0100Mbps to all households\xc2\xa0by 2019.The New New York Broadband Program, at a cost of $1 billion -- half from the state, with the remaining $500 million to be provided by the private sector -- would see it provide speeds\xc2\xa0four times greater\xc2\xa0than the Federal Communications Commission\'s (FCC) 25Mbps proposed minimum broadband download speed.\xc2\xa0 "Access to high-speed internet is critical to ensuring that all New Yorkers can reach their full potential in today\'s technology-driven world," Cuomo said at the time."We\'re launching the largest state broadband investment in the nation in order to make that goal a reality. This is a truly bold undertaking that will improve the lives of New Yorkers in every corner of the state, and I am proud to make it a priority of our administration\'s second-term agenda."Earlier in December, Akamai\'s State of the Internet report revealed that 44 of America\'s states now have average broadband speeds of\xc2\xa0above 10Mbps.The report revealed that the District of Columbia saw the highest speed increase for the year, growing 34 percent to a 19.5Mbps average. New York, Virginia, New Jersey, Maryland, Washington, Rhode Island, Massachusetts, Utah, and Delaware all had average speeds of above 14.8Mbps.The global average, meanwhile, reached 5.1Mbps.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 In Australia, private telecommunications provider Telstra has similarly been\xc2\xa0upgrading phone booths\xc2\xa0to provide a AU$100 million national Wi-Fi network known as Telstra Air.The Wi-Fi service is only free to use until June 30, 2016, however, with only Telstra mobile and home broadband customers able to access it.Telstra\xc2\xa0launched its Wi-Fi network\xc2\xa0in June 2015, after turning\xc2\xa02,600 of its public phone booths\xc2\xa0into Wi-Fi hotspots.The Wi-Fi network also makes use of Telstra hotspots at retail stores and customers\' own homes, allowing customers to use their home broadband data allowance while away from the home.\xc2\xa0 Source: ZDNet\nFEATURED SPOTLIGHT\nLatest Updates\nFollow @PipelineWire\n\xc2\xa9 All information contained herein is the sole property of Pipeline Publishing, LLC. happened to "Think Different" @ Apple.Google\xe2\x80\x99s grab for the sidewalk has begun with the rollout of LinkNYC free public Wi-FiNew York is finally getting its promised 5G gigabit Wi-Fi as the city starts\nupgrading payphone booths with the latest tech thanks to a public-private partnership that Google managed to get a slice of in an\nacquisition made earlier this year.Starting with a beta test today, up to 10,000 kiosks will get equipped with a touchscreen tablet for free internet and calls, a USB charging point and free Wi-Fi up to 20-times faster than the average broadband service.The advertising-funded Wi-Fi has been touted to work within a 150 foot radius and users can jump from hub to hub as they travel through the city.Credit:\nLinkNYCWhat looks like the first booth to be modified,\nat 15th St and 3rd Avenue, means the city is sort of making good on its promise to start the rollout in 2015, but only just!The plan was first\nannounced back in 2014 after a\ncompetition created by the former Mayor\xe2\x80\x99s office to transform the city\xe2\x80\x99s street furniture for the 21st century.The scheme has hit a few snags over the past year, including\naccusations that poor neighborhoods will get slower speeds because advertisers will be less willing to sponsor booths there.Buzzfeed also\nconducted an investigation that saw the company behind the booths, Intersection, having to remove planned Bluetooth devices that would serve ads directly to people\xe2\x80\x99s phones as they walked by.A similar attempt to do this in London, via smartphone tracking Bluetooth bins, was\nhalted after concerns were raised by privacy campaigners.Intersection was created through a merger of the two companies delivering LinkNYC and was then\nacquired by a consortium of investors led by Googles\xe2\x80\x99s Sidewalk Labs urban innovation company.The Labs launched in June this year and this is its first project to go live.A spokesperson from Sidewalk Labs told TNW that although tests have begun, the booths will not actually go live to the public until early next year.Report TOU ViolationApple, Inc. More to come \xe2\x80\xa6 #smartcities #technology #wifi #nyc #3rdavenue\nA photo posted by LinkNYC (@linknycofficial) on Dec 29, 2015 at 8:51am PST\nNew York City announced its plan to transform phone booths to Wi-Fi hubs\xc2\xa0in November 2014, but it wasn\xe2\x80\x99t until this week that\xc2\xa0workers\xc2\xa0began installing the first access point, near Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s Union Square. Expect about a week or two of beta testing before New Yorkers can use the hubs to get online.\nThe city will get about 500 more hubs by mid-July.\xc2\xa0When the project is completed, roving city dwellers should be able to hop from Wi-Fi hotspot to Wi-FI hotspot\xc2\xa0as they (and their smartphones) travel through the metropolis.\nThe Wi-Fi hubs are expected to bring in $500 million in advertising revenue for New York.\n(Via The Verge)\nRecently on GOOD\nWhat does the dust in your home mean for your\xc2\xa0health?\nYou vacuum it, sweep it and wipe it off your furniture.
